  3. The Schick Hydro 5 has two main advantages over my usual three-blade razors -- either the Gilette Mach 3 or the store brand from Target, depending on how ready I am on a given day to start throwing the big bucks around. First, the shave is noticeably smoother. Second, I suppose because the cutting work is spread out over more blades, they last significantly longer.<br /><br />I confirmed these results, as I did when testing another five-blade razor, the [[ASIN:B005ACNPKA Remington King of Shaves Azor 5 Blade]], by dividing my shaves halfway down my face and using this razor on one side and a brand-new Target store brand on the other. Even when brand new, this razor feels smoother than the three-blade. After a few weeks of usage, the difference was very noticeable for me.<br /><br />On the negative side, I find the Schick Hydro 5 awkward and bulky when doing what I need to do. I maintain a beard, and I need a razor to do three things: keep my neck clean and define the lower line of my beard at the jaw, shave the few little hairs that grow wolfman-like up my cheeks at the top of the beard, and keep the back of my neck clean shaven. The back of the neck is fine, but the large size of the shaving head makes it more difficult to keep a straight line maintained at the bottom of the beard. With the more manageable and finely maneuverable three-blade head, shaving a straight line at the neck is a snap.<br /><br />Others have spoken about the hydrating gel. I honestly can't speak to that. I use shaving cream, and all I really notice is that the razor is cutting under an eighth of an inch of foam. I can't speak well as to what gel is coming out of the razor at the bottom of all that foam, and I don't see how others could either.<br /><br />So the bottom line is yes, five blades does make a difference as far as I can tell, in terms of both a smooth, comfortable shave and longer lasting razors. However, if your aim is to keep a beard trimmed, you'll do better with a smaller, higher-precision razor head.<br /><br />I think if I shaved my whole face, I would prefer this razor over the three-blade heads I generally use.gher-precision razor head.<br /><br />I think if I shaved my whole face, I would prefer this razor over the three-blade heads I generally use.

I am not much for brand loyalty or fall for the hype of multi-blade designs but truly, the Hydro series is a razor for the discriminating man and woman who shave regularly and sensitive to any irritation that comes from doing it.<br /><br />The Schick Hydro for men (re-branded [[ASIN:B00AHF1GTM Hydro Silk for women]]) is the most recent razor redesigns that now feature five blades and heavily modified lubricating strip that stays wetter longer, producing an effortlessly close shave comparable to the [[ASIN:B00AGEW0AI Gillette Fusion]] (a alternate five blade design). Well it might something that many men have resigned themselves to expect, the burn was different after the Schick Hydro - I felt it wherever I shaved and I cannot help to wonder that now these multi-blade designs are in fact shaving more skin as well. Instead of having the distinct trimmer of the Fusion or [[ASIN:B0056GOHN4 Quattro]] designs, Schick engineers went for a flip-top design that moves the lubricating strip (the blue strip) away from the razor head and locks that in place - it takes two hands to do it, which may not be that that simple if they are large or wet.<br /><br />Nevertheless, it is an awesome razor and leaves an incredibly smooth and effortless shave. The transparent design - you can see through in-between blades - ensures that it rinses out well as it dries out, providing the same experience for weeks to come. My first use with the blade was like this. The second and subsequent times I wielded the same stone cutting blade, a few tiny petrified saplings remained, but I had to use the tip of my most delicate finger to trace out their roots. Not bad. Indeed. And if you've ever cut timber with a blade, you'll concur that sometimes getting that sawdust stubble out of your blades can be frustrating, sometimes even forcing you to bang your blade on the edge of your sink like Thor pounding his hammer. Not so with this razor. That's a good thing, as sinks are expensive to replace.<br /><br />Now to round it all out. I would have loved to have a 1/2 star option on this one because I was in between the &#34;middle&#34; ground of the 3 and the &#34;almost hallowed&#34; ground of the 4. But like salaries and employee rankings, I personally like to be rounded up, so I paid this one forward...barely. Why? Outside of the misleading packaging, I get up, shower, shave, rotate with the kids' carpool, go to work. Yes, that is the essence of many a routine. But how much different could my day be, if when I shave (the most manly part of my morning, as I'm working a razor blade across my face!), I went on an adventure? How about picking up a chrome/steel/gray color handled blade and prepping myself to go save the planet on a mission to Mars? Or how about grabbing my Hulk green razor and prepping for my day as a superhero? Instead I got this fairly lightweight, nearly baby blue handled razor to wield like the man I dream of being. Call me what you like, but I want my razor to look the part. Just because I've traded my convertible for a kid-hauler doesn't mean that I want to be whisked away to the spa when I'm shaving. If I go to the spa, it's to get a massage to repair my broken body from all that superheroing I do all day. So yes, even my razor should take me on an adventure, and if not an adventure, I will gladly take a quest. Economy<br />I have to wait and see how long the razor lasts before I can answer this<br /><br />Detailed Review<br /><br />Testing Methodology<br />I tested this razor against a Gillette 3 blade disposable razor that I currently use, it has no hydration and is pretty cheap, I didn't shave for two days, and I only used water on my face<br /><br />I tested the Hydro on the left, and the Gillette on the right, I did one pass per side and then compared, repeating until I felt I couldn't do any better.<br /><br />Closeness<br />The hydro felt so smooth and comfortable that I thought for sure that it would win this test, it seemed to cut like a hot knife through butter.<br /><br />The Gillette in comparison felt like it was skipping and pulling at my face.<br /><br />When I finished pass one though the Hydro had left a LOT more of my beard on my face!<br /><br />The reason ( I think, test two will confirm ) is that the Hydration actually worked against the Hydro, it lubed my whiskers so well that some of them were lying flat and the blade just skipped over them.<br /><br />I washed my face and flicked the hydration bar out of the way, once that was accomplished I did more passes until both sides were as clean as I could get them and I have to say the Gillette still edged out the Hydro, I want to try this again without the Hydration bar and switch face sides before I pass a final judgement.<br /><br />Quickness<br />If you use the Hydro bar right out of the gate compared to a none hydrating razor it's going to take longer if your beard lays down like mine did<br /><br />Quite a bit longer since I had to clean my face for the final pass to get all the stubble off, in general the Hydration worked TOO WELL! In fairness my beard is fairly fine, and if your is stiff you might not have the same issue.<br /><br />Razor loading and cleaning between passes seemed about the same, I need to retest to be sure though.<br /><br />Comfort<br />If you use the hydration bar the Hydro wins hands down, extremely comfortable shave even just using water!<br /><br />Economical<br />More testing is needed, I am using the same two razors and will continue to test one against the other.<br /><br />Typically by shave 3-4 the Gillette becomes too dull to continue to use, and by shave 5 I toss it.<br /><br />I will have to run each blade to exhaustion to see how they compare cost wise.es until both sides were as clean as I could get them and I have to say the Gillette still edged out the Hydro, I want to try this again without the Hydration bar and switch face sides before I pass a final judgement.<br /><br />Quickness<br />If you use the Hydro bar right out of the gate compared to a none hydrating razor it's going to take longer if your beard lays down like mine did<br /><br />Quite a bit longer since I had to clean my face for the final pass to get all the stubble off, in general the Hydration worked TOO WELL! So now you have at a minimum six blades being pushed down and drug over the same spot with practically no lubricant. This is what produces the irritation, and essentially renders this razor nothing more than another cheap gimmick not worth its own weight (which as mentioned earlier is practically nothing anyway).
